VIX at 18.4 and the 10Y-2Y spread at +0.5% suggest a market in transition rather than crisis — not cheap enough to be a generational buy, not expensive enough to call a top — but with CPI at 3.3% limiting Fed flexibility and unemployment beginning to drift, any negative earnings surprise cycle could push VIX above 25 quickly. Long-term, normalised yield curve plus healthy corporate FCF generation in our selected names argues strongly for 3-5 year compounding from current prices.

The market is making two compounding errors simultaneously: pricing high-quality SaaS and royalty-model businesses as if rates will stay elevated forever, and treating profitable growth compounders that have sold off 50-80% as if they are broken businesses. In reality, the yield curve has normalised (+0.5%), inflation at 3.3% is sticky but decelerating, and several of the most cash-generative software and royalty franchises in the market trade at PE ratios that assume zero growth — a profound and correctable mispricing. The opportunity is to own businesses with 20-50% FCF margins and structural moats at multiples that were last seen in 2013.
1. HALO Halozyme Therapeutics · Healthcare HIGH ACT NOW Quality Compounder

"The toll road buried inside a pharma company — 13 pharma giants pay Halozyme every time a drug gets injected under your skin"

The market prices HALO as a speculative biotech when it is actually a fee-based royalty technology licensor: Halozyme's ENHANZE platform is now the de facto standard for converting IV biologics to subcutaneous delivery, and 13 partners including Roche, J&J, and Pfizer pay royalties on every commercial dose sold — without Halozyme bearing a single dollar of clinical trial risk. With 58% operating margins, 46% FCF margins, 38% revenue growth accelerating from 22%, and a PEG of just 0.7, the market is mislabelling a royalty compounder as a binary biotech bet. ROIC of 24% sustained on near-zero tangible assets is the clearest proof this is a capital-light franchise hiding in plain sight.

Price $68.05 PEG 0.7 P/E 25.3 ROIC 23.6% Catalyst 2026 pipeline of new ENHANZE partnership announcements plus royalty ramp from recently approved subcutaneous oncology indications (J&J's Darzalex SC, Roche's Tecentriq SC) should drive two consecutive quarters of earnings beats through mid-2026, forcing analyst estimate revisions upward. Watch A major partner drug facing a post-market safety withdrawal would directly reduce royalty revenue and would be the clearest thesis-breaker — monitor FDA safety communications for HALO-partnered drugs quarterly.
2. QLYS Qualys, Inc. · Technology HIGH ACT NOW IV Discount

"The most profitable security company nobody talks about — 46% FCF margins at 15x earnings while the market frets about growth rate optics"

Qualys generates more free cash flow as a percentage of revenue than most companies generate in gross profit, yet it trades at PE 15 — a 50%+ discount to software peers — because 10% revenue growth 'looks slow'. The market is confusing a royalty-like cash machine for a stagnant legacy vendor: Qualys is structurally embedded in enterprise compliance workflows (SOC2, ISO, PCI) where ripping out the platform means re-certifying every control, creating switching costs that would take years and millions of dollars to overcome. At 74% DCF margin of safety, 28% ROIC, and a net cash position, this is a business being valued as if it will shrink — it will not.

Price $85.17 PEG 1.6 P/E 15.4 ROIC 28.1% Catalyst Q2 2026 earnings cycle (expected late July) where conservative management guidance gets revised upward — consistent pattern of beat-and-raise against sandbagged guidance — should trigger institutional re-accumulation at a stock sitting at 55% of its 52-week high. Watch A sustained move by CrowdStrike or SentinelOne to build natively competing compliance modules at lower price points would structurally threaten QLYS's pricing power — monitor vendor consolidation trends in the CNAPP space.
3. DUOL Duolingo, Inc. · Technology HIGH WITHIN WEEKS Turnaround

"Duolingo crossed into GAAP profitability while growing 39% — the stock at 18% of its 52-week high still prices it as a pre-profit startup"

Duolingo achieved something rare in consumer tech: it became durably profitable (GAAP, not adjusted) in 2024 while sustaining 39% revenue growth and expanding FCF margins to 36% — yet the stock sits at 18% of its 52-week high as if the business deteriorated. The market has not repriced the structural shift from 'burning cash to grow' to 'compounding cash while growing' because the narrative lag in consumer tech is always 2-4 quarters behind the financial reality. With PE of 11 and a 75% DCF margin of safety, the market is paying almost nothing for what is now a global consumer subscription franchise with 500M registered users, AI-enhanced personalization that improves engagement and retention automatically, and no meaningful competitor operating at scale.

Price $98.78 PEG 0.7 P/E 11.1 ROIC 9.4% Catalyst Q2 2026 earnings report (expected early August) should confirm AI-driven subscription monetization is expanding paying subscriber ratios above Street estimates — DAU growth plus family plan penetration are the two numbers to watch for a re-rating trigger. Watch If AI language models (ChatGPT, Google Translate) begin offering interactive conversation practice at consumer-friendly price points, Duolingo's competitive moat in oral/conversational skills becomes genuinely threatened — this is the single risk that could permanently impair the thesis.
4. DOCS Doximity, Inc. · Healthcare HIGH WITHIN WEEKS Stalwart

"The LinkedIn of medicine with 80% of US doctors and 49% FCF margins — trading at 31% of its high as if pharma advertising just disappeared"

Doximity's platform reaches over 80% of US licensed physicians — a verified, credentialed, captive professional audience that pharma marketers cannot reach at this scale through any other single channel. The market sold off the stock to 31% of its 52-week high during a pharma ad-spend slowdown, but the fundamental business never broke: FCF margins remained 49%, the balance sheet is debt-free with 20% net cash to price, and revenue growth has now re-accelerated from 13% back to 20%. With ROIC of 20%, 90% gross margins, and zero debt, this is a near-perfect quality compounder being priced like a cyclical ad business at trough.

Price $23.90 PEG 1.6 P/E 18.7 ROIC 20.5% Catalyst Q1 FY2027 earnings in May 2026 should confirm pharma advertising recovery is durable and not a one-quarter bounce — guidance for FY2027 above consensus will be the specific re-rating trigger given how deeply the stock has been de-rated relative to fundamentals. Watch Customer concentration risk is real — if 2-3 top pharma advertisers consolidate or cut HCP marketing budgets simultaneously in response to drug pricing legislation, the revenue recovery could stall and the thesis timeline extends significantly.
5. MNDY monday.com Ltd. · Technology HIGH WITHIN WEEKS Turnaround

"Monday.com crossed into GAAP profitability with 27% growth and 40% of market cap in cash — the market still prices it as a pre-profit startup"

MNDY achieved the structural inflection investors wait years for — GAAP profitability in 2024 while sustaining 27% revenue growth, 89% gross margins, and FCF conversion of 2.7x — yet it sits at 21% of its 52-week high with a forward PE of 8.2x versus a trailing PE of 28.5x. The disconnect is extreme: the market is pricing last year's narrative (loss-making SaaS) against this year's reality (profitable, cash-generative enterprise software). With 40% of market cap in net cash and zero existential risk on the balance sheet, MNDY has the firepower to accelerate AI product development and enterprise upsell while competitors with weaker balance sheets retrench.

Price $65.43 PEG 1.6 P/E 28.5 ROIC -0.1% Catalyst Q1 2026 earnings in May with continued enterprise upsell momentum (net revenue retention above 110%) and AI-driven seat expansion announcements should catalyse institutional re-accumulation — the specific number to watch is enterprise customer cohort growth above 25%. Watch Revenue growth is decelerating (from 33% to 27%) — if Q1 2026 shows further deceleration below 22%, the 'profitable growth' thesis weakens materially and the 8x forward PE may still not be cheap enough to justify the position.
6. HIG The Hartford Financial Services · Financial Services HIGH WITHIN MONTHS Quality Compounder

"The best P&C insurer nobody watches — 28% ROIC, 15% FCF yield, PEG of 0.8, and the market still prices it as a commodity insurer"

The Hartford has spent a decade building proprietary risk-pricing models in specialty commercial lines — workers' comp, professional liability, management liability — that produce underwriting discipline that cyclical commodity insurers simply cannot replicate. The market prices all P&C insurers as interest-rate proxies and commodity underwriters, completely missing HIG's 28% ROIC and 50% margin of safety. At PEG 0.8 and PE 10, you are buying 12% annual earnings growth at a price that assumes zero multiple expansion — just the earnings growth alone makes this a 12% annual return floor without any re-rating.

Price $138.75 PEG 0.8 P/E 10.1 ROIC 28.2% Catalyst Q2 2026 earnings in late July should confirm commercial pricing cycle continuation and reserve releases from workers' comp lines — combined ratio improvement toward 90% would force analyst upgrades from a sector trading at the cheapest PEG in the market (Financial Services PEG 1.2 sector average vs HIG at 0.8). Watch A catastrophic loss year (hurricane, earthquake, cyber) that forces reserve strengthening could temporarily impair earnings and interrupt the compounding story — the 2026 Atlantic hurricane season (June–November) is the key exogenous risk to monitor.
7. ADBE Adobe Inc. · Technology HIGH WITHIN MONTHS Quality Compounder

"The creative cloud that runs every professional designer on earth — 37% ROIC, 89% gross margins, and a PEG of 1.5 at a decade low relative valuation"

Adobe has somehow been re-rated from 'unassailable creative monopoly' to 'AI disruption victim' despite no evidence of meaningful customer attrition — its Creative Cloud and Document Cloud platforms are embedded in every professional design workflow on earth, and switching costs are immense because the files, workflows, and training are Adobe-native. The market is pricing a scenario where generative AI tools commoditise design — but Adobe is shipping Firefly AI natively into Creative Cloud, meaning AI enhances rather than displaces its platform. At PEG 1.5 and 37% ROIC with 42% FCF margins, this is textbook Lynch: a dominant franchise at a price the market would not have offered you at any point in the past five years.

Price $244.66 PEG 1.5 P/E 13.9 ROIC 37.4% Catalyst FY2026 Q2 earnings (expected June 2026) where Firefly AI monetisation through Creative Cloud add-on pricing shows initial attach rates — any evidence of successful AI upsell above Street estimates should trigger multiple expansion from a stock at 58% of its 52-week high. Watch Accelerating Figma adoption in the enterprise UI/UX segment combined with continued Canva penetration in the SMB creative market could compress Adobe's addressable seat growth below 8% annually — monitor churn metrics in the Creative Cloud subscriber base for any deterioration.
8. DLO DLocal Limited · Technology MEDIUM WITHIN MONTHS Fast Grower

"The only payments infrastructure that actually works across 40+ frontier markets — 47% growth, 29% ROIC, and almost nobody in the West follows this stock"

DLocal is the infrastructure layer that makes it possible for global merchants (Uber, Netflix, Amazon, Shopify) to collect and disburse payments in 40+ markets across LatAm, Africa, and Asia where local banking rails are fragmented, currency controls are complex, and fraud risk is elevated. There is no Western equivalent — building this from scratch requires 5-10 years of local regulatory relationships, bank partnerships, and fraud models in each market. With 47% revenue growth accelerating from 15%, 29% ROIC, 37% FCF margins, and a PEG of just 0.9, DLocal is priced as if it is a commodity payments processor when it is actually the only player with genuine first-mover infrastructure advantages in markets that represent the next 3 billion internet users.

Price $13.53 PEG 0.9 P/E 20.3 ROIC 28.5% Catalyst Q2 2026 earnings (expected August) where Total Payment Volume growth trajectory confirms continued 40%+ organic expansion plus new merchant wins in Africa and Southeast Asia — any disclosed partnership with a Tier-1 global merchant new to the DLocal network should drive institutional accumulation. Watch A major emerging market currency crisis (Argentina, Nigeria, or Turkey) combined with DLocal's FX exposure could produce a quarter of compressed take rates that the market would interpret as structural margin deterioration — monitor FX hedging disclosures closely in each earnings report.

⚠ Key Risks

  • HALO + QLYS royalty/SaaS re-rating could stall if macro deteriorates and PE multiple expansion fails to materialise despite strong FCF — the thesis needs multiple expansion, not just cash generation, to deliver near-term price performance
  • DUOL + MNDY at 18-21% of 52-week highs face continued retail capitulation risk if tech sector sentiment deteriorates on Fed hawkishness — even great businesses can go lower in a risk-off VIX spike to 30+
  • DOCS pharma advertising recovery thesis breaks if large pharma cuts marketing budgets in a recession — revenue re-acceleration from 13% to 20% reverses quickly if the one key customer concentration risk materialises
